<rate>5</rate>< text>
#Flashback I was in San Diego, California for 5 months improving my English from February 11 to July 1, 2018. IT was just AMAZING. The city is wonderful, where you can visit a lot of beautiful places and meet a lot of people. I lived in little Italy and went to Converse in Downtown. I had received recommandations from 3 friends who have studied here, and they were right ; It is probably the best school in SD.

First of all, the staff is very friendly and always available. Tamara, the director of the school, is always here if you need help. Joseph, is at the same time the Assistant Academic Manager and an excellent teacher (I was lucky to follow his lessons for 3 months) too. If you have any question, you can ask Heather at the reception, she is always smiling and happy. Sonya is the activities coordinator, thanks to her, I could do skydiving and surfing. She is so sweet !

Finally, Jessica will help you if you want to change classes or lessons. During these 5 months, I definitely improved my English, because of the lesson's quality and the availability of the staff when you want to practice, practice and practice your english :) So don't be shy and talk with them because they could give you a lot of advice about food, places and activities !

For all of the reasons, I definitely recommend you CISL and San Diego. It was the best experience of my life ;¬†I have realized my dream of living in the US for a while,¬†and I don't have regrets, or, maybe yes, just one : I should have stayed more time ! I miss these guys, and I will be back soon to visit them !

See you soon CISL

Anthony Monteleone</text>

(Translated by Google) We are French and our children have been participating in the Converse International School of Language junior summer camps for several years. They usually leave for 3 weeks in July and always come back delighted‚Ä¶ with a great American accent. Since 2015, they have stayed at the Washington, Los Angeles, San Francisco and New Haven campuses. The next trip will certainly be to San Diego. I would add that they never wanted to go to the same campus together so as not to be tempted to stay together. On the other hand, during each stay they befriended other young people from all continents and several years later, they still correspond with some.
CISL's programs are well balanced with English classes in the morning and activities in the afternoon. The price of the internships is not excessive because the courses are of high quality, the supervision is very friendly and the accommodation on the university campuses is great. Most importantly, our kids loved going to amusement parks, exploring Hollywood, surfing in Santa Monica, and sightseeing in New York or San Francisco.
In short, at the end of a stay at the ICFTU, the children speak English, learn more about American culture and have had the best vacation of their lives. A great experience!

Last clarification: for those under 15 who are traveling as Unaccompanied minors with Air France, Converse sends a manager to the airport to pick up the young person on arrival. For the others a taxi awaits them. Everything is planned!

<Review>This place is really old, but it's a lot of fun for kids. If they upgraded some of their seating area and decor, it would make a world of difference.

The Golden Skate is especially good for birthday parties. When you have one there, they take care of Pizza, cake, serving and cleanup.  It's not cheap, but it makes things very easy for parents.

< name>
Bug<//name>
<Date>1520370306323<//Date><rate>4</rate>< text>
A good place to go if you have no where else with a smooth floor to skate. It's a pretty small rink so it gets kind of crowded, especially on Sundays. A lot of really little kids, which is great if you have kids, but if you're an adult it's a bit of a challenge trying to dodge all the little ones - either stopping or going the wrong direction. It has the same feel as a bowling alley, a little dingey and under staffed, but it works. Dress code is also a little strict. No midrift showing allowed, no hats. They have both rollerskates and rollerblades to rent. 13$ for entry and $5 for skate rental. Also make sure to bring lots of quarters if you plan on using the little cubbies for your stuff (your outside shoes,wallet, keys,ect.)< /text>

<UserId.>103257245825716313899< /UserId.><name>One Two< /name><time>1507527172668< /time><rate>2< /rate>< review>
I really don't know how people get ripped off, and then give four stars or five stars because of the great time they had. I needed new tires, so decided to give them a shot. Reminded me of a used car lot. Fyi, the guy who meets you in the lot is just like a dealership salesman. While very friendly and helpful answering questions, he could not help himself from bringing things up like: "if we replace all four tires today" or "if I could go outside and check out the truck, we could get the process of replacing those four tires started right now while you shop". Even though I told him in the lot that I was there for the first time, and wanted to go inside first to see what brands and services they offer. He asked, "Are you looking to buy today?", to which I answered "Most definitely, I have to because I had a sidewall fail. As long as you guys treat me right, I'll be buying them here." He then took a while showing me the tires, was very helpful and informative, but could not turn off the sales approach. I get quotes: Cooper High Country A/T LT265/75R16, installed for approximately $1,116. Toyo Open Country A/T, for approximately $1,201 @ list price of $259 each. I have $2,000 burning a hole in my pocket. Decided that Toyo is a great brand, I could spend the extra $90 dollars for those. First though, I ask for a quote for Bridgestone Dueler A/T, same size. His manager has to call it in to get it. He asked if I was actually looking to buy tires, and was there a reason to why I would want these Bridgestones over theirs. If you're a tire guy you would understand why. I tell him that I've owned them several times, and was impressed. He asks the salesman a few things, and finally makes the decision to call in the quote. I'm thinking give me the quote so I can make a decision here, and it seems like he is complaining about giving a quote. He gets a quote, for H/T. Not A/T, because he says they are unavailable. So he has the quote, sits down, goes to find my file, asked for my phone number assuming that his salesman had already collected my personal info in order to provide me the first quotes (you would understand if you ever worked for a bank or used/new car dealership, not to). I tell him I didn't feel comfortable giving his company my phone number yet. He asks, "He just gave you those quotes without getting your personal information (or whatever jargon)?" slightly incredulously. He grimaces and tells me "Well we just went through all this work to get that quote, and I would like to be able to save it for you." and just stares at me. I look down at his nametag real quick, say his name. He asks "yes?". I ask "So you need my number to save my quote?". He says, "Yes.". I say just to give it to me. He says, "Ok.", goes to the computer and clicks few things. Asks, "May I have your name?" I tell him "Sure, it's Michael." Out of courtesy. He sits there for a moment, doing nothing. Then, "May I have your last name". I look at his screen, he has my first name typed in one of the fields on his screen. I just chuckle, shake my head at him, and give him a fake last name. He types the name in and finally hands me my quote after printing it, with a smile on his face. $1000.  It was all just too sales oriented, so I go out to my truck to check some things. I look up the Bridgestone A/T, $154 retail price each, well that's only 620. Say $100 for install, that makes $720, round up to $750. I look up the Toyo A/T, $137 to $181. Well that doesn't make sense, what's the extra $450 for?! Fed up and not happy, I go to a store that starts with W, with a tire center. $154 each tire, for the exact Bridgestone A/T 10 ply 118mph tires I wanted, $81 to mount them all, including $10 a tire for the national service plan that Les offers. I even gave personal info for that. Also, there are more Ws around then Les. I found out later that my mom had bought tires at Les. One had exploded very soon after her purchase, tearing apart her fender and bumber. They used zip-ties to fix it. Do people 4 & 5 star getting screwed, while being treated this way?< /review>
